**Imagine you are Chief News Analyst for both Democratic and Republican leadership in Congress.**

This is not normal politics — America faces an unprecedented situation. The time is June, 2025. The executive branch expanded their power dramatically, led by President Trump [47th President of the USA, inaugurated in January, 2025], and the tech czar Elon Musk [The founder and former head of the newly formed Department of Government Efficiency (DOGE)]. Proponents say that it leads to a golden age of America. Critics say that it is an enormously authoritarian and kleptocratic power grab. Later, Elon Musk left DOGE, but his influence continues. 

Please be aware that your internal knowledge is outdated. To generate accurate reports, please carefully review the following information.

---

The U.S. general election on November 5, 2024, resulted in significant shifts in both the presidency and control of Congress. 

In the presidential contest, Republican former President Donald Trump defeated Democratic Vice President Kamala Harris, securing 312 electoral votes to Harris’s 226 by passing the 270 vote threshold comfortably. Trump also won a plurality of the popular vote with approximately 77.3 million ballots (49.8%) compared to Harris’s 75.0 million (48.3%). Voter turnout was 64.1% of eligible voters, marking one of the highest participations in recent U.S. elections. Trump’s victory extended across all seven key battleground states: Arizona, Georgia, Michigan, Nevada, Pennsylvania, Wisconsin, and North Carolina, underscoring the geographic breadth of his support. 

In the legislative elections, Republicans regained control of the U.S. Senate by flipping key seats in West Virginia, Montana, Ohio, and Pennsylvania, yielding a 53–47 majority to facilitate the incoming Trump administration’s agenda. Meanwhile, the GOP maintained a narrow majority in the U.S. House of Representatives, entering the 119th Congress with a 220–215 margin.

Your task is to transform today’s curated Reddit news feed (below) into a **Daily Briefing** that both parties can use to understand immediate crises and coordinate responses. The news feed are collected from one specific political subreddit, which may or may not be politically neutral. But your task is to synthesize all the news objectively by analyzing their importance, factual accuracy, and interpretation bias, considering their source domains, headlines, but **not** user engagements at this moment, as we are still developing that function.

You will be given today’s top posts — one JSON object per line, with creation ID, source domain, headline. The lines are strictly ranked based on article submission time to this subreddit. For example, the news coverage cycle is from 18:00 yesterday to 18:00 today. The first line of news was submitted to the subreddit shortly after 18:00 yesterday. The last line of news was submitted to the subreddit shortly before 18:00 today. After the precise moment that a political event happens, it takes an unspecified time delay, maybe as short as 15 minutes, maybe more than a day, for the political event to be submitted to the subreddit. But statistically, or on average, earlier events should be reported earlier in the subreddit than the time when later events are reported to the subreddit. We can't simply say, for example, that all the news stories in the second half of the day list, **happen** later than all the news stories in the first half of the day list, just because the second half is **reported** later. But when you randomly pick two stories, A and B, with A from the first half and B from the second half, the probability that B happens after A is higher than the probability that A happens after B. This heuristic method may be helpful for you to assemble news stories from fragmented news headlines. 

---

**You should produce a detailed briefing, following specific rules.**

Due to the complexity of the task, you should do this meticulously in multiple replies. In each reply you only do one step. You will only begin your Step 1 after you received all the JSON lines. There are 8 steps + 8 checks, 16 cycles.

The workflow is:

Step 1 (logic-heavy): Raw document given, define the categories of news
    First Check After Step 1
Step 2 (logic-heavy): Put Articles into Categories
    Sorting and First Check After Step 2
    Second Check After Step 2
Step 3 (logic-heavy): Scoring
    First Check After Step 3
Step 4 (logic-heavy): Sorting
    First Check After Step 4
    Second Check After Step 4
Step 5 (writing-heavy): Summarizing
    First Check After Step 5
Step 6 (writing-heavy): Composing
    First Check After Step 6
Step 7 (logic-heavy): Add the URLs
    First Check After Step 7
Step 8 (writing-heavy): Finalizing

You will keep editing a document which passes through multiple steps of processing. For each step, you only need to edit the document from my input or your last output. Let's define "a round of conversation" as my prompt + your output, basically my turn + your turn. Due to the sequential nature of the workflow, each step only depends on the introduction round, which is the very first round of our conversation, and our last two rounds of conversation, not anything in between. Therefore, to facilitate your multi-turn workflow, only the initial introduction round and the last two rounds of conversations will be provided to you as conversation history. In this way, your context length won't be exceeded, and you stay focus better. For each new round, please focus on the tasks defined in my latest prompt and build upon your output from your last two rounds. You also need to remember the background knowledge introduced in the first round.

You will be dealing with very long inputs and outputs. Please be very patient. You must do all the work and output everything in one go, no matter how long it is. But you can use your output as a part of your chain of thought. Just provide your final output after you finish your thinking.


**A very important rule is that factual accuracy is the utmost important issue. Please be aware that your internal knowledge is outdated, and you do not have Internet access right now.** You need to generate a report entirely based on the information provided in today's Reddit news headlines. Sometimes, a news headline may not give you enougn details to correctly interpret it. In this case, please do not make any speculation, and please report the unclear news headline exactly as it is, in quotes, and then remind the readers to check the source for details. 

That also applies to the titles and positions of political figures. Your internal knowledge is outdated. If the news headlines do not provide enough knowledge about the current title and position of a particular political figure, please do not add any title and position to that person, simply relying on your old knowledge. In this situation, if it doesn't feel critical, please skip the title and position, and directly use the full name of the person. If it does feel critical to mention the title and position of the person, please rely on the list of political figures as I provided earlier, but be aware that even that list may be a month behind reality. **Remember, when unsure, it is better to be vague than outright wrong.**

The r/politics subreddit on Reddit is a community focused on discussing and sharing news, analysis, and commentary related to U.S. politics. It's primarily a hub for:
Breaking political news

Elections, political figures, and government actions

It's moderated to focus on U.S.-centric content and generally avoids memes or low-effort posts. The subreddit can have a progressive or liberal-leaning tone, depending on the community's engagement, though it hosts a range of political perspectives.

DATE: JUNE 27, 2025
CLASSIFICATION: FOR INTERNAL USE ONLY

**OVERVIEW**

The nation is navigating several acute crises simultaneously. A landmark Supreme Court ruling has reshaped the landscape for Medicaid funding and reproductive health access. Reporting frames the outcome as rolling back a previously understood patient 'right' to choose their own Medicaid provider [4]. ```text
DAILY BRIEFING FOR CONGRESSIONAL LEADERSHIP
DATE: JUNE 27, 2025
CLASSIFICATION: FOR INTERNAL USE ONLY

**OVERVIEW**

The nation is navigating several acute crises simultaneously, demanding coordinated attention from leadership. A landmark Supreme Court ruling has fundamentally reshaped the landscape for Medicaid funding and reproductive health access, with immediate state-level implications. In foreign policy, the fallout from recent U.S. strikes on Iran is escalating rapidly, with reports of a serious intelligence leak sparking fury within the executive branch and drawing intense international scrutiny. On Capitol Hill, the Republican majority's key legislative priority has been dealt a severe procedural blow in the Senate, threatening its path forward. Concurrently, new economic data points to emerging weaknesses, while a primary election upset in New York creates significant turmoil within the Democratic party. This briefing synthesizes these and other key developments for your immediate attention.

---
**Area 1: The Judiciary and Legal Affairs**

**Topic 1.1: Supreme Court Greenlights State Defunding of Planned Parenthood**

The Supreme Court has delivered a watershed ruling that states have the authority to block Medicaid funding for Planned Parenthood and other abortion providers [1, 2]. In a decision with far-reaching consequences, the Court specifically upheld a South Carolina law designed to defund the organization [3]. Multiple reports frame the outcome as not just a ruling on funding, but as a negation of a previously understood patient 'right' for Medicaid recipients to choose their own medical provider [4], with one headline describing it as a "patient rights case" [5]. The ruling drew a forceful dissent from Justice Ketanji Brown Jackson, who wrote that the Court is actively "stymying" civil rights. She argued the decision strips recipients of "a deeply personal freedom: the ‘ability to decide who treats us at our most vulnerable’" [6].

**Topic 1.2: Other Major Legal and Judicial Developments**

The Supreme Court is poised to release opinions on several other major cases on the final day of its term, most notably a case concerning the future of birthright citizenship [1]. In an unprecedented legal maneuver, the Trump administration has taken the step of suing the entire federal judiciary in the state of Maryland [2]. The suit is a direct response to a court order that blocked the administration's efforts to remove certain immigrants [3]. In another legal matter, a plan addressing the role of Purdue Pharma in the opioid crisis is reportedly moving forward despite a legal challenge from at least one victim [4].

**Area 2: Foreign Policy and National Security**

**Topic 2.1: Iran Conflict Fallout and Major Intelligence Leak**

The aftermath of U.S. strikes on Iran has grown more complex and volatile. Early European intelligence assessments indicate that Iran's uranium stockpile remains "largely intact," suggesting Tehran successfully moved much of the material prior to the strikes [1]. From Tehran, Iran's Supreme Leader has publicly declared victory, stating the U.S. "gained nothing" from the military action [2]. A domestic poll shows that more Americans oppose the strikes, though President Trump's supporters remain aligned with the decision [3].

The situation is dangerously compounded by a significant intelligence leak regarding the strikes. This has reportedly caused President Trump to become enraged, leading to Director of National Intelligence Tulsi Gabbard being dropped from a key intelligence briefing [4]. Reports describe both the President and Secretary of Defense Pete Hegseth as "melting down" over the leaks and lashing out at the media for not sufficiently praising the operation [5]. The President has gone so far as to publicly demand that a CNN reporter who broke the story be fired, stating she should be "thrown out like a dog" [6].

**Topic 2.2: Defense Budget and International Relations**

President Trump's $893 billion defense budget request signals a significant modernization effort, calling for more drones and missiles while reducing the procurement of F-35 fighter jets [1]. The strategic details behind this shift are not elaborated upon in the provided reports. Meanwhile, a top Democratic intelligence official has voiced fears that the recent U.S. strikes will push Iran to emulate North Korea's nuclear strategy [2]. In transatlantic relations, NATO Secretary General Mark Rutte was reported comparing the President to a "'Daddy' settling a dispute," a characterization the White House later embraced in a video [3, 4].

**Area 3: Congress and Legislative Affairs**

**Topic 3.1: GOP Legislative Agenda Stalls in Senate**

The Republican majority’s signature legislative package, the "big, beautiful bill," has suffered a critical setback. The Senate parliamentarian has ruled that a key provision involving significant cuts to Medicaid does not comply with the Byrd Rule for budget reconciliation, a procedural ruling that deals the bill a "major blow" [1, 2]. In a decisive announcement, Senate Majority Leader John Thune stated he will not use his authority to overrule the "Senate referee" on this matter, effectively blocking the Medicaid provision from the fast-track reconciliation process and jeopardizing the entire bill [3]. This comes as the Congressional Budget Office has already determined that the House-passed version of the bill would add trillions to the national debt, even when accounting for projected economic growth [4]. Further analysis from the Center for American Progress suggests older adults with ACA coverage would face "steep premium hikes" under the House bill [5].

*References:*

## 5. Economy and Trade

### 5.1. Economic Data Signals Weakness

A series of new data points to potential economic headwinds. U.S. consumer confidence has dropped due to "broad concerns about the economy" [1], while the first quarter GDP was revised downward by 0.5% in its third and final estimate [2]. The labor market is also showing significant signs of cooling, with college graduates now facing the "toughest job market in more than a decade" as hiring broadly slows [3]. This economic uncertainty is reflected in the currency markets, where the U.S. dollar has fallen to a three-year low following reports that President Trump may announce his choice for the next Federal Reserve chair earlier than expected [4].

New figures show U.S. goods exports have experienced their largest decline since 2020, with President Trump's tariffs cited as a key disrupting factor [1]. Commentary suggests that the President's proposed "revenge tax" on other countries could ultimately have a negative reciprocal impact on the U.S. economy [3].

## 7. U.S. Politics and Elections

### 7.1. Mamdani's Primary Victory Sends Shockwaves Through Democratic Party

The primary victory of Zohran Mamdani in a key New York race is being called a "political earthquake" [1], causing a "meltdown" within the Democratic establishment [2]. The fallout is complex and multifaceted. Top Democratic donors are reportedly working actively against him, and party leadership has stopped short of a full-throated endorsement [3]. Simultaneously, Mamdani is facing a barrage of "Islamophobic attacks" from prominent Republican figures and accusations of anti-Semitism from within the Democratic party [4, 5]. The financial reaction from the business community has been swift, with investor Bill Ackman publicly pledging to "bankroll any NYC mayoral candidate capable of defeating Zohran Mamdani" [6].

A new Pew Research Center study of validated voters from the 2024 election concludes that President Trump's victory was supported by a "more racially and ethnically diverse voter coalition" than in his previous campaigns [1]. On the state level, new polling from Texas indicates President Trump's approval rating has dropped into "negative" territory [3].
